## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The governing equation encodes restoring forces (nonlinear in x), damping (possibly nonlinear in v), and potential external driving (periodic in t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 + c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic velocity): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type dissipation)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring force)
- Position-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (coupling between position and velocity)
- Driven van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 + c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect in symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms (x²) in restoring force break symmetry and shift the equilibrium — expect in asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type limit cycles)
- Periodic functions of t (sin, cos) without x or v coupling indicate external harmonic driving forces
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v, x²*v) indicate nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies
- Cubic restoring terms (x³) with opposite sign to linear term (x) indicate a double-well potential (Duffing bistability)
- Absence of velocity terms indicates a conservative (Hamiltonian) system with energy conservation

GT Equivalence Verification (PO36)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidate formulas: 51

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `0.156063*sin(t) - 0.372948*v*exp(-|x|)`.

The key challenge is the `exp(-|x|)` term. This equals `exp(-x)` for x≥0 and `exp(x)` for x<0. No single `exp(cx)` term can replicate this behavior for all x, since `exp(cx)` is either always increasing or always decreasing in x.

Let me analyze the candidates systematically:

**Candidates with simple `v*exp(cx)` terms (most candidates):**
Candidates like 1, 2, 20, 23, 43, 44, etc. contain `v*exp(c*x)` which gives a single exponential. Setting c=-1 would match for x≥0 but not x<0. So a single `exp(cx)` cannot match `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(cx)+1)` terms (9, 29, 48, 12):**
`log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)` - for large positive c8*x this approximates c8*x, for large negative c8*x this approaches 0. This doesn't produce `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `(c+x)^c` terms (18, 19):**
Power functions can't replicate `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `v/(c+x)^2` or `v/(c+x)^5` terms:**
These are rational functions and can't replicate `exp(-|x|)` either.

**Candidate 16, 28: `v*log(c*x²+1)`:**
`log(c*x²+1)` is an even function of x, which is promising since `exp(-|x|)` is also even. But `log(c*x²+1)` grows logarithmically while `exp(-|x|)` decays exponentially. Combined with `v*exp(cx)`, we'd need `log(c*x²+1) + A*exp(Bx)` to equal `C*exp(-|x|)` which isn't possible.

**Candidate 45: `c5*exp(c6*x + c7*v) + c8*v*exp(c9*x)`:**
The `exp(c6*x + c7*v)` term mixes x and v nonlinearly through exp, which doesn't help since the GT is linear in v.

**Candidate 33: `v*exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*x + c9)`:**
This introduces oscillation in x, which `exp(-|x|)` doesn't have.

**Candidate 9: `c5*v*x + c6*v*log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)`:**
For the log term: if c8 > 0, log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1) ≈ c8*x + log(c7) for large x, and ≈ log(1) = 0 for large negative x (if c7>0). This is like a "soft ReLU" - not exponential decay.

**Key insight:** `exp(-|x|)` is not analytic at x=0 and is an even function. None of the candidate formulas contain `|x|` or `Abs(x)`. The question is whether any combination of the offered terms can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` for all x.

No finite combination of polynomials in x, single exponentials `exp(cx)`, logarithms, power functions, or rational functions of x can equal `exp(-|x|)` for all real x. The function `exp(-|x|)` has a kink at x=0 and specific exponential decay in both directions, which requires either the absolute value function or a sum of infinitely many terms.

Even candidates with multiple x-dependent terms (like polynomials + exponential) cannot match because:
- A single `exp(cx)` decays in only one direction
- Polynomial and rational terms have different asymptotic behavior
- `log` terms grow rather than decay

None of the candidates can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` for all values of x.

[NO MATCH]

2) A \(v\cdot e^{-|x|}\) term (even in \(x\)), coefficient \(-0.3729...\).

4) Conditional equivalence is allowed: since \(e^{-|x|}=e^{-x}\) on domain \(x\ge 0\) (or \(e^{x}\) on \(x\le 0\)), any candidate with \(v e^{k x}\) can match on one side by choosing \(k=-1\) (for \(x\ge0\)) or \(k=+1\) (for \(x\le0\)).

Also, \(\sin(c1\,t+c2)\) can match \(\sin(t)\) by setting \(c1=1, c2=0\) (or other phase choices that reduce exactly to \(\sin(t)\), e.g. \(c1=1,c2=2\pi n\)).

**Candidate 3:** Has `v/(c7+x)²` and `v*x²` terms. Set c0=0, c4=0, c5=0, c6=0 (to zero v/(c7+x)² need c6=0), c9=-1. Result: `c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c8*v*exp(-x)`. ✓

**Candidate 4:** Has `v/(c4+x)⁵`. Set c3=0, c5=0, c6=0, c9=0, c8=-1. Result: `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c7*v*exp(-x)`. Wait, need c3=0 to zero the `v/(c4+x)⁵` term. ✓

**Candidate 5:** Has `v*log(c6*x+1)`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 6:** Has `v/(c6+x)²`, `v*x²`, `v*x`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=0, c8=-1. Wait, c5=0 zeros `v/(c6+x)²`. ✓

**Candidate 7:** Has `v*log(c6*x+1)`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 8:** Has `c7*x` (not multiplied by v). Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c7=0, c9=-1. ✓

**Candidate 9:** Has `v*log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1)`. This is a softplus-like function. Can we make it equal to `v*exp(-x)`? No — `log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1)` cannot equal `exp(-x)` for all x. But we can set c6=0 to eliminate this term. Then we have `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v + c4 + c5*v*x`. This gives `sin + linear_in_v_and_x`, which cannot match `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 11:** Same as 4 structure. Set c3=0, c5=0, c6=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 12:** Has `v*log(c8*exp(c9*x)+1)`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0. Left with `sin + c7*v*log(c8*exp(c9*x)+1)`. This softplus cannot equal `v*exp(-x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** Set c3=0, c5=0, c8=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 14:** Set c3=0, c5=0, c8=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 15:** Has `v/(c4*t+c5)` — depends on t. Set c3=0, c8=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 16:** Has `v*log(c6*x²+1)`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 17:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3 + c4*v*exp(c5*x) + c6*v*x + c7*v + v*x`. The `v*x` term has coefficient 1 (fixed!). Cannot be zeroed. Need c6 = -1 to cancel, giving `c0*sin + c3 + c4*v*exp(c5*x) + c7*v`. Set c3=0, c7=0, c5=-1. ✓

**Candidate 18:** Has `v*(c6+x)^c7`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=-1. Left with `sin + c8*v*exp(-x)`. Wait, need c5=0 to zero the power term. ✓

**Candidate 19:** Has `v*(c8+x)^c9` with coefficient 1 (fixed!). Cannot be zeroed. This term is always present. Unless c9=0, making it `v*1 = v`, then set c3 to absorb. So: set c9=0, then `v*(c8+x)^0 = v`. Combined with c3*v: `(c3+1)*v`. Set c4=0, c7=0, c3+1 → set to 0 (c3=-1), c6=-1. Result: `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c5*v*exp(-x)`. ✓

**Candidate 20:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 21:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 22:** Set c0=0, c4=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 23:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 24:** Set c3=0, c7=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 25:** Has `c8*x`. Set c3=0, c5=0, c8=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 26:** Has `c7*x`. Set c3=0, c7=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 27:** Has `c0*x`. Set c0=0, c1=0, c2=0, c3=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 28:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 29:** Has `v*log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1)`. Set c3=0, c5=0. Left with `sin + c6*v*log(...)`. Softplus ≠ exp(-x). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 30:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c8=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 31:** Set c3=0, c5=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 32:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 33:** Has `v*exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*x+c9)`. Set c3=0, c5=0. Left with `sin(t) + c6*v*exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*x+c9)`. Need `exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*x+c9) = exp(-x)`. Set c8=0, c9=π/2, then sin(π/2)=1, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 34:** Set c3=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 35:** Fixed `v*x` term. Need c6=-1 to cancel. Set c3=0, c5=-1. ✓

**Candidate 36:** Set c3=0, c4=0, c7=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 38:** Set c3=0, c6=0, c9=0, c8=-1. ✓

**Candidate 39:** Set c3=0, c6=-1. ✓

**Candidate 42:** Set c3=0, c7=-1. ✓

**Candidate 43:** Set c4=-1. ✓

**Candidate 45:** Has `exp(c6*x+c7*v)`. This is `exp(c6*x)*exp(c7*v)` — nonlinear in v. Set c5=0, c3=0, c4=0, c9=-1. ✓

**Candidate 46:** Set c5=0, c4=-1. ✓

**Candidate 48:** Has `v*log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1)`. Set c0=0, c1=0, c5=0. Left with `sin + c6*v*log(...)`. Softplus ≠ exp(-x). **NO MATCH**
